# 🧹 Base de Conhecimento — BookingKoala

> [!info] Sobre este vault
> Posts e comentários do **grupo privado do BookingKoala no Facebook** (snapshot de 21/06/2026), organizados por tema **a partir da análise do conteúdo real** — não de categorias genéricas. Cada entrada traz o post original, métricas de engajamento, as respostas capturadas da comunidade e o link da fonte.

## 📊 Visão geral

- **Publicações:** 1205  ·  **com texto:** 1203  ·  **com respostas:** 650
- **Reações somadas:** 0
- **Tipos:** 📝 1065 · 🖼️ 104 · 🎥 21 · 🔗 15
- **Categorias temáticas:** 19 (derivadas da análise de termos e tópicos do corpus)

> [!tip] Como usar com IA
> Carregue este arquivo como contexto e pergunte em linguagem natural, ex.: *"Como configurar pagamento de 50% ao provider sobre o valor com desconto?"*, *"Qual o custo por lead típico no Google LSA segundo o grupo?"* ou *"Como o pessoal lida com danos causados por cleaners?"*

## 📖 Glossário de termos recorrentes

- **BK** — BookingKoala — software de agendamento/gestão para empresas de limpeza.
- **L27 / Launch27** — Concorrente; muitos migraram do Launch27 para o BK.
- **Jobber** — Outro software de field service citado em comparações.
- **Thumbtack (TT) / Angi** — Plataformas de leads; estratégia comum é trazer o cliente para dentro do BK.
- **LSA** — Google Local Services Ads ('Google Guaranteed') — principal fonte de leads para muitos.
- **GBP** — Google Business Profile — perfil no Google Maps; crucial para SEO local e reviews.
- **Stripe** — Gateway de pagamento padrão integrado ao BK.
- **IC / 1099** — Independent Contractor — prestador autônomo (vs employee/W-2).
- **Provider / Cleaner** — Quem executa a limpeza.
- **VA** — Virtual Assistant — atende ligações/agenda.
- **GHL / GoHighLevel** — CRM/automação de marketing; 'Lead Connector' é o app dele.
- **n8n / Zapier / Make** — Automação para conectar o BK a outros sistemas via API/webhook.
- **Quo** — Ferramenta de reviews/automação citada pela comunidade.
- **STR / Airbnb** — Short-Term Rental — limpeza de aluguéis de temporada.
- **CAC / CPL** — Custo de Aquisição de Cliente / Custo por Lead.
- **Unassigned folder** — Pasta de jobs não atribuídos onde cleaners podem 'pegar' serviços.

## 🚀 Primeiros Passos & Novos no BK

_Quem acabou de assinar o BK ou está começando no ramo: setup inicial, conseguir o primeiro cliente, dúvidas de iniciante._  ·  `#comecando`  ·  **37 publicações**

### 1. Hi everyone Just joined, and I really appreciate this group and everyone who shares advice here…
📝 **Georgina Lowe**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2143677766186797/)

> Hi everyone
> Just joined, and I really appreciate this group and everyone who shares advice here. Reading through posts so far has been super helpful while starting out.
> I’m starting a remote cleaning business and have no professional cleaning experience besides normal day-to-day cleaning at home. There’s so much conflicting information online about products, techniques, procedures, etc.
> My biggest concern is hiring. Since I’m not an experienced cleaner, how do I properly evaluate cleaners or weed out “bad” ones outside of a test clean? I know test cleans help, but I’m more wondering how you learned to identify quality cleaners when you yourself were still learning.
> I’m also curious about checklists/SOPs. In the beginning, did you create your own systems and checklists, or did you mostly rely on whatever processes/products your cleaners already used?
> Would appreciate any advice or insight from anyone willing to share their experience!

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **April Lynn Kowalsky** 📈Colaborador em ascensão · 👍3: My advice is to join a cleaning group on Facebook, like the maids network, or Cbf, there's plenty of groups out there to lear…
  - ↳ **Adam Johnson:** feel free to Dm me will be glad to help
  - _(+6 respostas no thread original)_

### 2. Hi All, I'm brand new to the cleaning business and just getting started…
📝 **Chelsea Harrison Ramm**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2012848832603025/)

> Hi All, I'm brand new to the cleaning business and just getting started. Thank you all so much for the amazing contributions to the page, I am leaning so much.
> I need a little hep. My #1 fear in this business is getting cleaners to join my team. The logical part of my brain "gets" it. I understand the business model and how it works. But the irrational part of my brain just can't get on board. I have every excuse imaginable to not reach out to cleaners to start the process of onboarding them, and I am very aware that these excuses are irrational and fear based but I'm struggling to move past them.
> It would be awesome if you all could share positive stories around cleaners who love working with you all, how many cleaners you went through to find your dream team, how many rejections you got before you got a team on board, etc. I need to "see to believe" right now that if you all can do it then I can do it.

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Chelsea Perehudoff** 📈Colaborador em ascensão · 👍7: It’s not an easy business but when you find good people pay them well and treat them with respect
  - ↳ **Alex Swetnam:** You'll hear dream stories and nightmare stories from everyone.
  - _(+1 respostas no thread original)_

### 3. I wanted to share a win with you all…
🖼️ **Angel Juarez**  ·  🖼️×7  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1925509848003591/)

> I wanted to share a win with you all. October was our best month to date, closing at 200K for the month. We were able to land two huge housing projects, one of which I bid and closed literally a day before flying out on vacation. I’ve been gone since mid October, seeing the Colosseum in Rome, the Acropolis in Athens, the Eiffel Tower in Paris, and most importantly, the blue roofs in Santorini which has been my moms dream destination. I let my team know that they would have limited access to me, and over the last three weeks I have only worked a total of 5 hours roughly. This is my first time sharing a big win in this group I think, and I hope it doesn’t come off as bragging, I just wanna show everyone what’s possible. Having a great team is so important, if I didn’t have such an awesome team none of this would be possible. I hope you are all crushing your goals, we have two months left in Q4!

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Aqeelah Rahim** · 👍37: That’s a MAJOR win, congratulations
  - ↳ **Sharon FlaKa Martins:** Congratulations!
  - _(+70 respostas no thread original)_

### 52. Good evening fellow business tycoons…
📝 **Francis Clase**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2046152189272689/)

> Good evening fellow business tycoons. Quick question. We've been paying for the Better Business Bureau, probably going on three years, and honestly I'm questioning the value.
> The leads that we get from them are normally terrible, and they're not frequent at all. Actually, yesterday or the day before, we got a scam. Someone wanted to pay us $700 for a cleaning where we quoted them $300. One of those check-scam things, and it's like, "Okay, this is coming from the Better Business Bureau," and they normally don't even respond back. You call them, and most of the time they don't pick up.
> We're talking about it could be months before we get a lead. It's like every quarter, every three months, every four months that one comes in. If they converted, they would add some sort of value, but they never convert.
> Their system, the way they handle even cleaning leads, is also confusing. Some of the house ranges they give are like 1,500 to 2,500 sq ft, so it's like you don't even know what you're walking into. It's not really designed with house cleaning in mind; it's just kind of all over the place.
> Sometimes, to the point where we literally call and email them in that manner. Some of them want email; they want super high standards and the lowest prices possible. It takes a lot of time to go through that.
> We actually offer our pricing on the website, and it honestly feels like we can't even tell if these are real leads at times. We don't even know if they're real customers. They're not asking any sort of questions regarding discounts, how many cleaners are included, or whether something is included in a deep cleaning. It's like they just put in a quote, and that's pretty much it. There's nothing else. There's not even any sort of sign that shows us this is someone who's really interested.
> Sometimes the number doesn't even work. Even when it does, they'll say something like, "Alright, let me see what that looks like," and that's the end of it.
> At times, somebody will put in a quote for something months out. I remember this happening where someone submitted a quote saying they needed a cleaning five or six months from now, and they never followed through.
> Keep in mind, we've been using them for three years.
> We're paying about $600 to $700 a year for the badge, but it seems like the Better Business Bureau is more of a place where people go to complain rather than actually look for a service that's accredited. I don't know, maybe it's different for other industries, but we can't say it's the same for cleaning.
> No one really cares too much about the accreditation or that we have an A+ rating.
> I think in the three years we maybe had one customer who cared about the Better Business Bureau.
> Actually, it was interesting. I can remember a time where we had one customer who was interested because we had the Better Business Bureau, but this was somebody who didn't even sign up. He was like, "Oh yeah, that's why I'm calling you, because you're accredited by the Better Business Bureau," and he never even committed, so it's like maybe one lead, maybe if that.
> Now we're having a hard time really understanding the value this thing is actually bringing to us, and there's probably only one other cleaning company in the area that we see who's had it for as long as we have.
> At the end, we're questioning if it's even worth paying for it at this point, or if it's really adding value to our customers.' thoughts?

### 53. Admins Please remove of not ok to share here Gonna Share some personal stuff here I don’t think…
📝 **Tina Servis**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2017213428833232/)

> Admins Please remove of not ok to share here
> Gonna
> Share some personal stuff here
> I don’t think people understand how draining it is to run a cleaning company when you’re still in the field.
> It’s not just cleaning.
> It’s cleaning while:
> • answering client texts
> • handling reschedules
> • covering call-out
> • dealing with complaints
> • trying to recruit
> • trying to do invoices
> • trying to do quotes
> • trying to do EVERYTHING
> And for me… it hit different at least I think it did
> Because I was a single mom with two young kids who still needed me.
> I remember being so tired I’d sit in my car after a job and just stare…
> Because I knew I still had 10 more things to do when I got home.
> And it wasn’t even “business stuff.”
> It was:
> • homework
> • sports
> • dinner
> • baths
> • bedtime
> • life
> But at the same time… I’d have 3 in-person quotes lined up.
> So I was literally forced to choose:
> Spend time with my kids…
> or figure out a way to support them.
> And that mess was breaking me
> That’s when I realized something…
> I don’t have a “getting clients” problem.
> I have a capacity problem.
> Because I was the cleaner AND the owner…
> Every new client was just more pressure.
> So I started rebuilding my business differently.
> Little by little… I shifted into a referral-based model where I wasn’t the one doing the cleaning.
> And I’m not even going to lie…
> That’s when I finally started feeling relief.
> Not overnight.
> But enough to breathe again.
> Now here’s what I started doing that helped immediately:
> 1) I stopped doing in-person quotes for everything.
> If it’s a basic home, I realized I can price most of it with photos + a few questions.
> 2) I Raised my minimum fee
> The smallest jobs take the most energy and the least profit.
> 3) I built my schedule around my life — not my clients.
> I stopped letting people guilt me into times that didn’t work.
> 4)I treat my cleaners … like GOLD.
> Not with “pizza parties”… with pay, respect, and consistency.
> 5) I stopped trying to be everything.
> The cleaner, the office, the salesperson, and customer service
> I’m not saying it was easy but I can say after 19 years I’m still going and I live an amazing life.
> Hope this helps any of you that may be struggling like I did

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Powers of Clean** · 👍7: We think that is how all cleaning companies start. Until you grow bigger and take help. It isn't far fetched or out of the ord
  - ↳ **SunnyPenguin2066:** Currently starting the same as you did
  - _(+25 respostas no thread original)_

### 56. Hey everyone!…
📝 **Lucas Vieira**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2152912508596656/)

> Hey everyone! I've seen a few people here run into pricing issues in BookingKoala lately, so I figured I'd share the ones that trip people up the most:
> Frequency discounts aren't configured right
> A lot of people set weekly/biweekly/monthly discounts but they're not linked correctly, so customers get charged the same or more for a recurring service than a one-time. Open your frequencies and actually run a test booking for each one. You may be surprised.
> Your flat-rate price isn't based on real job time
> If you charge flat-rate, your profit on each job depends entirely on how long it actually takes. Price a job at $150 but it runs 6 hours instead of 4, and your margin evaporates. The fix isn't to stop charging flat, it's to base your flat price on accurate time estimates, and tie cleaner pay (hourly or % of booking) to that same estimate. Mismatched or guessed estimates are what kill margins.
> No square-footage scaling
> A 1,500 sqft deep clean shouldn't cost the same as 5,000 sqft. If you're not using unit-based pricing, you're either losing big jobs or underpricing them.
> Biggest tip: after ANY pricing change, run a full test booking start to finish. Most "I accidentally overcharged" problems come from never testing the live flow.
> For the experienced owners here, what's your #1 pricing rule you wish you knew on day one?

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Jazen Duane** · 👍1: Hi, is there a chance that you are looking for a Virtual Assistant?
  - _(+2 respostas no thread original)_

### 59. Hi everyone, I'm setting up BookingKoala for a residential cleaning company and I'm running int…
📝 **Llana Rillera**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2157501821471058/)

> Hi everyone,
> I'm setting up BookingKoala for a residential cleaning company and I'm running into an issue with estimated cleaning durations.
> Right now, it seems like the estimate is stacking based on bedrooms, bathrooms, and square footage all at the same time, resulting in cleaning times that are much longer than what would realistically be needed.
> For example, a home might be estimated at 8+ hours when the actual cleaning would likely take closer to 3–5 hours.
> Ideally, I'd like the estimate to be driven primarily by the home's square footage (or whichever method is considered best practice), rather than having beds, baths, and square footage all compound the estimate.
> Has anyone run into this before?
> What settings should I check?
> Service duration settings?
> Booking form settings?
> Rate modifiers?
> Bedrooms/bathrooms configuration?

## 🧽 Tipos de Serviço & Escopo

_Deep clean, move in/out, recorrente, comercial, Airbnb/STR, add-ons e o que incluir em cada serviço._  ·  `#servicos`  ·  **63 publicações**

### 111. Best Flat-rate Add-Ons?…
🖼️ **Mark Baker**  ·  🖼️×2  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1850359378851972/)

> Best Flat-rate Add-Ons?
> Looking to crowdsource easy, high-margin add-ons that:
> Take very little time
> Billed flat-rate
> Are profitable
> Are easy to execute
> Offer obvious value
> Customer is happy to say yes to
> Not looking for windows inside fridge and ovens as those are already something we do.
> Rather, simple, smart upsells that make the bill go up and the effecrive dollar-per-hour rate climb.
> For example, here is one we are about to test now:
> SLOW DRAIN CLEARING
> We use our drain cleaning tool to hook up hair and buildup from slow shower, tub and sink drains.
> $9.99/drain
> We use our drain cleaning tool hook out hair and other gunk from slow or clogged drains in showers, tubs and sinks.
> Pop up states we:
> Do not take anything apart
> Are not a plumber
> Do not guarantee results
> Customer pays for the attempt not outcome
> Generally provides significant improvement in flow
> We'll use the drain cleaning took from Home Depot that costs $1.78 for two and hook out hair and other gunk from slow drains.
> We''ll already be cleaning those surfaces anyway, so the process of using the tool takes about five minutes, with an added two minutes added to the total cleaning time for about 7 minutes per drain on the high end.
> MATH
> Here is the typical bill for my own home and what it would look like with the drains added, which I am going to do for my next booking.
> Small spllit entry bungalow, as shown. with three bedrooms, 2 full bathrooms, and small rec room. Other area downstairs is basement apartment not included in cleaning.
> Generally takes 3.5 hours for our standard checklist so here is how the bill normally looks:
> 3.5 hours × $36 = $126 service charge
> $11.99 product add-on
> $4.99 fuel surcharge
> $142.98 total before tax
> $25 tip
> $167.98 gross earnings
> $167.98 ÷ 3.5 = $47.99/hour effective rate
> Now add six drains with the tub/shower combo and sinks included and the double drain kithen sink included.
> 6 drains × $9.99 = $59.94
> 6 drains × 7 minutes = 42 minutes
> New total time: 3.5 hours + 42 minutes = 4.2 hours
> NEW BILL
> 4.2 hours × $36 = $151.20 service charge
> $11.99 product add-on
> $4.99 fuel surcharge
> $59.94 drain add-on
> $228.12 total before tax
> $25 Tip
> $253.12 gross earnings
> $253.12÷ 4.2 = $60.27/hour effective rate
> $12.98/hour increase in effective rate
> $85.14 Total gross earnings increase.
> Extra time 42 minute
> $85.14 Gross/hour while clearing the drains
> I would be extremely grateful to hear what other add-ons that we could add to our bookings.

---

### 112. Hey everyone, My name’s Chris, I run a cleaning business back in Canada that’s been operating s…
🔗 **Chris Hachez**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1852219101999333/)

> Hey everyone,
> My name’s Chris, I run a cleaning business back in Canada that’s been operating since 2020. Lately, I’ve been realizing we may be undercharging compared to market standards, and I’d love to hear from those of you with more experience on the best way to move forward.
> Check us out here: https://maps.app.goo.gl/MRQcLxzj1Q7XaK4Q8?g_st=ipc
> A bit of background: my partner started cleaning years ago and some of those clients are still with us six years later. I came into the business in 2020 after leaving the military, and since then we’ve raised our rates from $35/hr to $45/hr. But from what I’ve seen in this group and through my own research, we’re still sitting low compared to others in the industry. We don’t upsell extras, everything is strictly time-based.
> Here’s our current breakdown:
> • Standard Clean: $45/hr
> • Deep Clean: $55/hr
> • Airbnb: $50/hr
> • Move In/Out: $60/hr
> We pay contractors $25/hr (base) and $30/hr for move-outs.
> A couple of questions I’d love your input on:
> 1. Have any of you successfully shifted from hourly pricing to a different structure?
> 2. How did you introduce upsells or add-ons without scaring off long-time clients?
> On the backend, I’m running numbers using Jacques H. Bastien KPI scorecard to get a clear picture of where the business stands. I’m open to any advice, and happy to jump on a call if someone’s open to chatting.
> Current software stack:
> • QuickBooks: Accounting & invoicing
> • Zenmaid: Scheduling & staff management
> • Clean Genie: Automation, hiring, contracts
> • (Considering switching to Booking Koala—I’m not thrilled about paying ~$1,000/month to Zenmaid just because we’re over 20 providers.)
> Would really appreciate any thoughts, lessons learned, or strategies you’ve used that worked well.
> Thanks in advance!
> Chris

> I’m looking for some guidance from those familiar with sales tax in Washington or other states with similar rules. I’m currently preparing an invoice for our first floor and carpet cleaning job. Up to now, we’ve only handled recurring janitorial service contracts, but we’re starting to expand into more specialized cleaning services.

> Also, is it standard practice to structure invoices as:
> Service Amount + Sales Tax = Total Invoice
> We’re hoping to secure more and bigger contracts with this client after this initial service, and the tax portion can become significant on larger jobs. I’d really appreciate any insights, tips, or best practices from others in the industry.
> Example:
> $5,000 + $435 (8.7%) = $5,435 total
> Thanks.

### 174. Has anyone noticed that recurring online bookings DO NOT redirect to your thank-you page?…
🖼️ **Anatole Noskov**  ·  🖼️×1  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2039362983284943/)

> Has anyone noticed that recurring online bookings DO NOT redirect to your thank-you page?
> I've been troubleshooting a conversion tracking issue for the past week and finally found the cause. When a customer books a RECURRING service, they get the green "Congratulations! You booking has been completed. Please click here to sign in to your account so you can make any changes to future bookings". (See screenshot) popup but never get redirected to the thank-you page. It just dead ends. The redirect URL is set correctly in Booking Form Settings. I was only able to reproduce this issue with recurring bookings.
> One-time bookings still redirect, but with a long delay. The green confirmation popup appears instantly, customer assumes they're done and closes the tab before the redirect ever completes.The redirect to the thank you page takes about 4-5 seconds while the c ustomer is presented with a green popup "Thank You". They can easily refresh or close the tab before the redirect completes. Which kills your conversion tracking.
> This is a huge deal for anyone running Google Ads or Facebook Ads. If your conversion tracking fires on the thank-you page (like most setups), you are losing conversion data on every recurring booking. Your ads platform thinks nobody is converting even though bookings are coming in. You're essentially flying blind on your most valuable customers.
> I submitted a ticket but wanted to check here — is anyone else experiencing this? Did something change recently on BK's end?
> Two things that need fixing:
> 1. Recurring bookings need to redirect to the thank-you page again
> 2. The redirect delay on one-time bookings needs to be faster — or at minimum give us an option to skip the green popup so the redirect happens immediately
> Any workarounds appreciated. This is costing real ad dollars every day it's broken.

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Anatole Noskov** · 👍2: Why have I not heard from anyone in 72-hours? Does anyone  work at your company anymore? Why the  is there 0 communication??
  - ↳ **Ean Smythe:** Did you ever get an answer for this
  - _(+5 respostas no thread original)_

### 176. Hi everyone, looking for some advice from other BK users…
🖼️ **Alina Kalinina**  ·  🖼️×1  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1991762118045030/)

> Hi everyone, looking for some advice from other BK users.
> This isn’t the first time this has come up for us, so I’m hoping someone has found a better setup.
> We charge hourly for larger homes (over 3,000 sq ft). When we create an hourly service in BookingKoala and select a recurring frequency (for example, every 4 weeks), the system still automatically shows a frequency discount on the receipt, even though the service is billed strictly hourly and that discount does not apply.
> So the receipt ends up showing something like:
> – Service total
> – Frequency discount
> – Discounted total
> – Adjusted amount back to the original hourly price
> Which understandably confuses clients, and we’ve had several people email us asking why the frequency discount “wasn’t applied,” even though it shouldn’t apply to hourly services in the first place.
> My question:
> Is there any way to prevent frequency discounts from showing at all for recurring hourly services?
> Or a better way to structure hourly recurring jobs so clients don’t see the flat-rate frequency discount on their receipt?
> If anyone has found a cleaner setup or workaround for this, I’d really appreciate hearing how you’re handling it.

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Eddie Booth** · 👍5: I would try adding new frequencies without a discount that are only for the hourly service. I can show you if you want
  - ↳ **Spotless 'n Serene Cleaning Service:** Roger just took mine off my site.
  - _(+1 respostas no thread original)_

### 177. UpVote this Feature Request…
🔗 **Shawn McNamara**

> UpVote this Feature Request: The current monthly view provides a "Job/Booking Count" next to the calendar date. While a nice feature, it falls short. What would be better is to swap the "job count" for "total job hours booked" for that day.
> A typical house cleaner represents 6-6.5 labor hours per day. If a company has 10 workers available on a given day, that would represent 60-65 labor-hours of availability. If a given day then shows current scheduled labor-hours of 45 labor-hours, then we know we have space to plug a client in.
> As it stands now, just seeing "job count" tells us nothing. Tuesday could show 15 jobs that only represent 50 hours of labor, while Thursday shows 9 jobs that represent 80 hours of labor. This could cause someone to think that there's not enough room to book anyone on Tuesday and that Thursday has plenty of availability, which would be completely opposite of the truth.
> Total job hours (including unassigned jobs) would be a FAR SUPERIOR piece of data than just simply "job count".
> PLEASE, BK, make the change! (and everyone reading this, sign in to https://feedback.bookingkoala.com/ and vote this up.

---

### 180. Is there a way to lock a client’s recurring rate permanently so it never auto-changes?…
📝 **Alina Kalinina**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1962571970964045/)

> Is there a way to lock a client’s recurring rate permanently so it never auto-changes?
> We keep running into an issue where custom recurring rates (either higher or lower than our current pricing) eventually revert back to our standard website rate — sometimes after reschedules, and possibly after a certain amount of time.
> Examples:
> In September, we lowered our recurring prices by ~5%.
> However, we have long-term clients who should keep their original (higher) rate, and it should never be adjusted down.
> We also have monthly/recurring clients with custom rates (usually higher due to heavy clutter or extra time required). We manually adjust the rate and apply it to all future bookings — but later it reverts back to the default rate, especially after rescheduling.
> The problem is that as we get busier, this is very hard to catch unless:
> A cleaner flags it
> A client notices the price change
> Or we manually audit bookings (not realistic at scale)
> This causes payroll issues, client confusion, and under-charging.
> How are you handling this?

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Saleem Hourieh** ⭐Supercolaborador · 👍2: When you change the price, you are either changing the price for the service package or for the pricing parameters ()
  - ↳ **Jessica Michal:** It’s absolutely after x amount of time.
  - _(+1 respostas no thread original)_

### 231. Those using ICs…
📝 **Shawn McNamara**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1843173509570559/)

> Those using ICs: What sort of contractual terms are you including in your contract with them that acts as preventative measures against bad behavior (i.e. calling out, lateness to job, poor quality, etc.)
> I once heard of a company using ICs that financially penalized (by deducting from monies owed) the IC for last minute call-outs or no-shows to job, or perpetual lateness, etc. For call-outs, company would dock the IC $50 from what it owed the IC and used that $50 as pay-incentive to other ICs willing to take on the job last minute.
> Needless to say, that company's ratings & reviews on Glassdoor got shredded by irate ICs who didn't like the money being deducted from their weekly deposit but how else is a company to penalize contractors for bad behavior or poor performance (besides just getting rid of them)?
> Considering the fact that you can't treat ICs the same as employees, what sort of measures have y'all put in place to keep your ICs in line and adhering to standards and expectations?

## 👥 Equipe: Cleaners, Contractors & VAs

_Contratação, IC vs employee, comissão/payroll, test clean, background check, VAs e gestão da equipe._  ·  `#equipe`  ·  **117 publicações**

### 290. I failed hard…
📝 **Kirsten Boudreaux**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1880621452492431/)

> I failed hard. Let’s talk about it…
> I want to preface this by saying that I strongly believe failure is never wasted work in business. It’s actually one of the biggest tools that guides you toward success.
> I’m one of the most aggressive businesspeople you’ll ever meet, bar none. So when I set out to scale my business this summer, I went in with a plan, consistency, and investment. I started the summer with two VAs, a staff of about 12 cleaners, and a consistently full calendar for one of my locations.
> I smashed every goal I set, but here’s what happened:
> My admin staff wasn’t a good fit. Our ad dollars had no return. Oversight and SOPs didn’t help. I had to let staff go. Sales is such an important skill in this industry, if you can’t close over the phone, good luck making a cent. Meanwhile, cash flow was affected, which meant it was harder to invest more into ads.
> What I learned from this:
> Set up ironclad SOPs from the beginning and consistently monitor staff performance on the phones.
> Train your staff on how to overcome sales objections. (So important!)
> Monitor your finances and make it a habit.
> Did this suck? Absolutely. But this has been one of the most valuable lessons I’ve learned, and I’m grateful I learned it early.
> The second biggest failure in a service-based business? Hiring the wrong people. Running a remote 1099 model means finding trustworthy, reliable cleaners is everything. And I’ll be the first to admit: I ignored red flags I knew would come back to bite me, and they did.
> I was in such a rush to grow that I hired too quickly just to cover cleans, because I became the rainmaker. That’s all well and good… until you don’t have enough quality supply to cover your demand.
> The result? Our first two negative Google reviews, countless refunds, and way too much provider drama. All of which could’ve been avoided if I’d trusted my gut and slowed down.
> What I learned here:
> Implement a hiring system from day one.
> Never rush to hire- vet thoroughly and don’t ignore red flags.
> As you scale, make hiring a priority (not an afterthought).
> Trust your gut with who you allow into your business.
> Don’t worry, I’ve spent my fair share licking my wounds. But I’ve moved on, and while this really sucked in the moment, I now feel more equipped than ever. Business is the school of hard knocks, and these lessons always come at a price.
> And here’s the thing: the price is worth it. Because every failure sharpens you. Every mistake builds resilience. And every single challenge forces you to become the kind of leader your business truly needs.
> If you’re in the thick of failure right now, now is not the time to give up. Take the lesson, apply it, and keep moving forward. I’m proof that you can bounce back stronger, wiser, and more determined than ever.
> I’m an open book, feel free to ask me anything. And if you’ve had a failure that taught you something invaluable, I’d love to hear it. Let’s normalize talking about the messy parts of business, not just the highlight reel.

---

### 291. Government Contracts Don’t Fail Because of Capability…
📝 **Ebony Grey**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1994921354395773/)

> Government Contracts Don’t Fail Because of Capability. They Fail Because of Cash Flow.
> I see this all the time, especially with first-time and growth-stage contractors.
> A business gets invited to bid on a large federal or commercial contract. The opportunity is real. The scope is solid. The problem?
> No upfront deposit
> First payment 30–60+ days after performance starts
> Payroll, onboarding, background checks, training, and supplies must be paid before the government ever cuts a check
> This is where many businesses assume, “We can’t afford to pursue this.”
> That’s not always true.
> As a certified SCORE mentor and government contracting instructor, here’s what I want contractors to understand:
> Your contract is leverage.
> Banks, CDFIs, and specialty lenders will often underwrite based on the contract itself, not just your cash on hand.
> Your bank is your first stop.
> Ask about:
> • Working capital lines of credit
> • Contract-based loans
> • Bridge financing tied to receivables
> CDFIs exist for this exact gap.
> Community Development Financial Institutions can:
> • Provide working capital
> • Structure contract financing
> • Help you identify additional funding partners
> There are lenders that finance government contracts specifically.
> These firms use the awarded contract as collateral to fund:
> • Payroll
> • Onboarding
> • Startup and mobilization costs
> Invoice factoring stabilizes cash flow once billing begins.
> After your first invoice, factoring can advance 70–90% so you’re not waiting on federal payment cycles.
> Sometimes the smartest move is partnering.
> Prime-sub relationships or JVs allow you to perform without carrying all the financial risk.
> One critical reminder:
> Many federal contracts require W-2 employees, not 1099s. Misclassification can kill a contract before it starts. Always review labor clauses carefully.
> Bottom line:
> Federal contracting isn’t about having cash sitting in the bank.
> It’s about knowing how to structure capital around the contract.
> If you’re turning down real opportunities because of cash flow fears, it may be time to rethink the strategy, not the goal.
> #GovernmentContracting
> #FederalContracts
> #SCOREMentor

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Titan Office Cleaning Crestview** · 👍1: Thank you for this insight! Are you available for mentorship? May I send some follow up questions.
  - _(+4 respostas no thread original)_

### 294. Guide To Get FREE Facebook Leads Via Local Facebook Groups Attached is a guide for your VAs/you…
🔗 **Christopher Peterson**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1926115974609645/)

> Guide To Get FREE Facebook Leads Via Local Facebook Groups
> Attached is a guide for your VAs/your team to win leads in competitive Facebook groups.
> We have gotten A LOT of time and help from this group and generous business owners. Some of it has been gold and all of it is appreciated.
> Hopefully this is a small help back to all of you and something we’ve found a ton of success in.
> To note: We have spent less than $500 in paid marketing and run around $15-20K a month in revenue. Most of revenue is from these groups.
> The document below is from the perspective of a VA, but as an owner, below is a simple formula.
> Facebook (Owner role):
> Join local Facebook groups.
> Look for past cleaning posts
> When somebody new posts
> A) Post Hi (name) great service, reliable, and has local discounts for X town. @YourCompanyName
> 203-555-4321
> B share with team members via Facebook.
> C) They post and MUST all like the main initial post (this needs to be most or second most liked post
> You want 3-4 comments per post.
> Otherwise, Make sure if you as owner come in second, everyone likes that main post.
> - Types of groups to join: Mom groups, Parent groups, affluent areas help but all work.
> + The Facebook groups show a search icon on the top right. To know if it’s a good group - search “Clean” or “looking clean” “houseclean” and see what the last 5 posts have been.
> *If it’s only randos posting their cleaning company, and no locals asking, it may not be a good group.
> https://docs.google.com/.../19pQLdEF0WJHyYTSZtNTb.../edit...

### 299. Had a marketing service reach out that was charging $1400 a month to post in 200 local Facebook…
📝 **Alex Swetnam**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1903506393537270/)

> Had a marketing service reach out that was charging $1400 a month to post in 200 local Facebook groups... but Nextdoor posts and comments on other neighbors asking for recommendations wasn't included.
> They had good results for high-ticket clients, but with a business like house cleaning it's more difficult to justify the spend the first few months.
> I have spoken to a few in this group who have made tens of thousands through free lead channels like Nextdoor + FB Groups.
> I am creating a system and hiring a VA to scan FB groups and Nextdoor 3x a day, and use mine, his, my partners, and a friend's account to post/comment and then like our own post/comment so it goes to the top of the post out of all the other comments...
> I'm likely going to grab 4-5 other friends in my area with similar businesses that would benefit, so instead of paying a VA $1k a month we all can pay $200 each... Or, of course, I could charge each of them more and make it into an entire business... But baby steps first lol
> If anyone else is:
> 1. doing this at scale
> or
> 2. navigated having a VA do it instead of yourself;
> I'd love to chat for 10 minutes.

## 🎯 Marketing — Anúncios Pagos (Google/Meta)

### 407. After 5 years of starting and growing a cleaning business, I recently just signed the dotted li…
📝 **Yusuf Lewis**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1958639191357323/)

> After 5 years of starting and growing a cleaning business, I recently just signed the dotted line to sell it! I have officially exited my first business!
> Funny to think I stumbled across a Reddit post about starting a cleaning business and did everything that it said lol. Shout out Rohan and anyone who got started from that thread.
> It only felt right to make this post in the groups because this is where I lived in the beginning of the business. In these group I met great people who helped me and became mentors.
> This post isn’t a “how to start a cleaning business” or anything, just sharing a few things from my journey. If you have questions you can ask away!
> When I started, it was at the beginning of the “remote cleaning business” model era. It took me time to get the business started because I was in college. Once I cracked marketing, which was right before I graduated back in 2021, things began to roll.
> April 2021 I had my first 10-cleaning month. June I had my first 20-cleaning month and July we went up to 30 cleanings. I was all in on the business since then. It was my full-time job, but it was more like a full-time masterclass on business, MBA and the gulag you go through as an entrepreneur. I’m 26 years old now and since starting the business I’ve grown so much when I sit back and reflect. I’m no guru either! I’m from Detroit, I moved to Atlanta to go to Morehouse College, I started my cleaning business my senior year, and since graduating I’ve spent my life up to this point of writing this running the business.
> At the height of the business, which is when I decided it was time to sell, I had the business operating on a chaotic rope.
> I had residential cleaning customers and commercial contracts. At one point we had a number of Airbnb properties we did cleaning for and at another point operated all three at the same time. (Was a freaking zoo!) I had a great office manager named V who was the sweetheart and pitbull for me and the business. I had a great team & rolodex of cleaners who, after all the mayhem, worked with us for multiple years at a time. When it was time to ascend, we eventually got another star named J who was our sales rep alongside me.
> The business was at a point where a majority of the business was operating on a system and I checked on everything from my phone.
> This is the point where I decided to package up and get the business on the market for my own personal reasons.
> It’s so much that I learned from running a cleaning business, but these things are the most important that im about to share.
> Live and die by your cleaners.
> It took me years to understand why the cleaners are the most important part of the business. When I started I thought you could just hire a cleaner by the snap of a finger and when I did that I almost lost every time. The cleaners are the backbone of the business. They are the make or break point. It’s necessary to appreciate when you come across great cleaners and keep them busy. Understand that when customers hire a cleaning service that’s a very serious buying decision for them. Imagine a customer books you, you send an unqualified cleaner and the customer is unhappy and never books with you again. That’s what happened with me until I started bringing on good talent.
> Many will say the most important aspects of the cleaning business are marketing and you need to focus on growing, but the hidden marketing lever is having some Vini’s and Itsmenia’s on your team. That’s what I had. I had cleaners that people knew and loved. When you have that you can almost hit a money glitch. Literally your business can grow through word of mouth the proper way. The cleaners were most important. It’s a grind at first but once you find that space cherish and respect it.
> The power of niching is a great power!
> When I first started the business I used Thumbtack, I used Yelp, I passed out flyers, I DID EVERYTHING! It all brought in clients. We did whatever because I was hungry and I needed to pay the bills. I didn’t have any other job, I did the cleaning business full time, so if you called we were going to clean it. It took me until about year 2 to understand the power of niching.
> When I finally understood, it’s like we hit another money glitch. Business got a little easier and we gained more money that made complete sense! I figured out which customer we were going to serve. We had services tailored only to their problems and aligned our systems towards solutions for only the problems they had. When I did this people found us vs us looking for them. When things got slow of course we always got back out there and took whatever that made sense, but we stayed true to the niche we chose and that’s when I started benefiting and growing the biz.
> It will behoove you to become a local superstar!
> If you run any type of business and you get customers that are paying you cold hard cash and using your services or whatever you sell, pat yourself on the back! Because people online make it like getting customers in your business is easy the shit is not easy! It’s only when you finally crack it is when it becomes easy like playing a video game.
> What I realized is that you have to become a local superstar and get your business out there as much as possible. You need to shout and let everybody know what you got going on. IDC who it is because when you do, eventually you will become known for what you are doing. That’s what happened with me. I let everybody and their mother know about my cleaning business. Not only that, I invested heavily into my marketing skills.
> Here are the areas I can turn on with a push of a button (Facebook Ads, Google Ads and SEO, and Thumbtack and please don’t put me in a room full of people because I will get business from an event too). I will go over this in a moment. But becoming a local superstar and known for what you do is a compounding effort. If you take your business serious the support you get is the gift you receive from being undeniable. I lasted 5 years, you will be surprised how many people don’t even start. People will recognize you! People will need you and soon people will start calling you. It’s up to you to step to the plate and perform.
> You need flow.
> Whenever I expressed hardship in my business, my friend who also runs a million dollar + landscaping business would always say fill up your pipeline. A pipeline in business is 100% important and should not be approached lightly. I will say you need to approach this as if someone is trying to take literal food from your loved one’s mouth. As if it’s life or death because truly if you aren’t getting customers you will eventually go flat. This means you need customers coming in from multiple areas.
> What I did was have paid ads and organic flows. For each area I put a system in place. I learned over time each system and it wasn’t all at the same time either. It started with the platforms like thumbtack, then I got decent with organic social media, decent with paid ads (FB & Google Ads), then I met the Yoda of Online Marketing, SEO. I wasn’t good at the beginning but over time I got good at each stop, built a system around it and kept it going. I’m not saying go and do all of this because it’s time consuming.
> What I am saying is that each system that got built all went into either the residential pipeline or commercial pipeline. My main goal was to get new people in the doors that I can talk to. I kept my pipeline full!
> A glitch is letting people know on stage about your cleaning business at local events. I constantly went to business events around ATL and every chance I got I grabbed the microphone and introduced my business with everyone looking. At these events people have bumrushed me for my information, to the point where I had my iPad ready to collect info and sell on spot. Take that information and do with it what you will.
> Then I began to get the soulful nod that it was time for me to depart from the cleaning business. It was such a journey. I once read in a book that once you finally get your business to the point where it’s running without you and things change, you can become more motivated to continue to grow that business. Not me. I’m forever grateful to the cleaning industry and have no ill will towards it, but I was able to see that it was time to go elsewhere.
> The journey led me to the stop to sell my business and on Nov 3rd, after months of work to sell the business, a contract was signed! At that moment the relief I felt was so reassuring that I hit a money dance!
> I’m so happy to have been in the industry and started my business journey here!
> For all the cleaning business owners and aspiring, keep pushing! This is an industry that is in demand. A cleaning business is a business that can provide you with whatever you need during the time of your life. Need extra money? Pick up a few houses to clean. Want to build a multi million dollar cleaning business? You can literally sign a few contracts and be at a million with a cleaning business. It’s whatever you want it to be. Not saying it’ll be easy but the money is there!
> I wish you all luck! And if you read this far, thank you!

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Jayger McGough Tomasino** ⭐Supercolaborador · 👍14: Well done Yusuf!!
  - ↳ **Andrea Thompson:** Congrats!! Growing a cleaning business takes a lot!
  - _(+49 respostas no thread original)_

### 408. Is anyone else experiencing a big increase in cancellations lately?…
📝 **Alina Kalinina**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2022313114989930/)

> Is anyone else experiencing a big increase in cancellations lately?
> For the past few months, we’ve been losing more clients than we’re gaining. What’s confusing is that many of these clients have consistently left 5-star feedback, expressed how happy they were, and some have been with us close to a year.
> The pattern I’m seeing is strong price pressure. A lot of clients are asking to lower the rate or cut hours while still expecting the same scope of work. We try to adjust by rotating areas or modifying the scope, but overall it feels like many people just want to pay less right now.
> Our revenue has been steadily declining since November. I understand winter is slower and February is typically soft, but this feels more significant than normal seasonality.
> For context, we went to 20k/month within six months using mostly Facebook leads. As of right now, we are only using Meta ads. LSA in our area are extremely expensive and, for us, not worth it even considering closing rate.
> What I’m noticing lately is that many leads seem extremely price-sensitive. It feels like people expect solo-cleaner pricing rather than company rates.
> Also for context, we are at $55/hour. MaidThis in our area is at $59/hour, and there are companies charging $70+ per hour. So we are definitely not the highest-priced in our market. We actually lowered our rate slightly while many others increased theirs.
> Is anyone else seeing:
> • More cancellations from long-term happy clients?
> • Increased pushback on pricing?
> • A noticeable shift in buyer behavior from Meta leads?
> Would really appreciate hearing what others are experiencing and what adjustments you’ve made.

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Rohan Aurora**: 1. January is budget season. When wallets tighten, anything that feels like a "nice-to-have" gets cut first. …
- **Julio Olivares** 📈Colaborador em ascensão · 👍18: If it’s out of nowhere I would see what cleaner/s were were paired with the clients that canceled and identify any patterns.
  - ↳ **Rohan Aurora:** 1. January is budget season. When wallets tighten, anything that feels like a "nice-to-have" gets cut first.
  - _(+7 respostas no thread original)_

> wondering if its going to give us much higher quality candidates. downside is i could see a competing company in the area getting mad that they could see it as poaching their cleaners and trying to harm us in some way - trying to go for solo cleaners, not poach.

> Not how I do my marketing…

### 412. Unpopular opinion from someone making $50K-$60K a month…
📝 **Ryan Lund**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1631280217426557/)

> Unpopular opinion from someone making $50K-$60K a month.
> Fuck scaling in one location, grow in multiples.
> Seriously your ad spend will be used more, less competition the more you spread.
> I mean hell in some areas Molly maid and them have like 1000 reviews, how are any of you going to compete unless you have been in that area a long time.
> So spread out especially if you are new and bootstrapping this shit yourself.
> If you have money to lose for a year or so then sure scale to your hearts content but most don't have that privilege so spread out and grow your business with more locations.
> I'm sure people will tell you I'm wrong, I won't argue less comp for me then.
> Though the reality is google will spend your ad spend more and more people will see you if you get out in front of more people via more locations.
> Have a good day!

## ⭐ Marketing — Google Profile, SEO & Avaliações

_Google Business Profile, ranqueamento no Maps, SEO local e estratégias para conseguir reviews._  ·  `#seo-reviews`  ·  **57 publicações**

### 478. We grew to $10k/month recurring in 6 months…
📝 **Alex Swetnam**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1830360907518486/)

> We grew to $10k/month recurring in 6 months. We’re on track for a conservative $20k by the end of the year (and honestly, it should be closer to $30k).
> Here’s what helped us grow fast:
> 1. Call leads right away.
> We don’t wait. If someone is interested, we call them immediately and focus on building a relationship. For us, this is more than a business—we often pray with people on the phone because we see it as a ministry.
> 2. Thumbtack has been huge for us.
> I know a lot of people don’t like Thumbtack, but in our area it’s been great. LSA (Google Local Service Ads) is way too expensive here.
> 3. Google Business Profile (GBP) changed everything.
> Three weeks ago I spent time learning how Google Maps ranks businesses, updated everything, and almost overnight we started outranking companies with 5–10x more reviews. Since then, we get daily calls and bookings.
> Because of that, our cost per lead dropped from $70–90 to almost zero. We’ve had so many leads coming in that we actually paused almost all of our paid marketing. Right now we’re averaging 3–4 organic leads a day from Google and booking about 2 of them daily—without spending a dollar on ads.
> If we turned Facebook ads back on, we’d probably get another 4–5 leads a day at $15/lead, but for now we’re holding off until we can scale up our team and systems to handle it.
> 4. Learn the details inside and out.
> Being an advisor on the phone is important. We don’t just take orders from clients—we position ourselves as the expert and build a cleaning plan around their specific needs.
> 5. We turn people away often.
> For lack of a better term, we “vibe check” people. If someone doesn’t pass the vibe check, they’re probably going to be a problem client. I’d rather give that spot on our calendar to a client who will be a GREAT fit, not just an “eh, this should be fine” client.
> 6. We build for where we’re going, not where we are.
> I don’t build systems for today; I build systems that will handle where we’ll be in 3–6 months. Staying curious and seeking advice from people ahead of me has been huge. Wise people have a council they ask for opinions. Jacob Elijah has been an invaluable mentor and friend throughout our journey - Thanks bro
> For those of you that are newer, keep going! You can do this. Listen to the awesome people ahead of you!

---

### 479. If you want organic leads… Then you need to have a couple foundational SEO things down…
🔗 **Alex Swetnam**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1924763784744864/)

> If you want organic leads…
> Then you need to have a couple foundational SEO things down.
> We went from paying $150 per closed booking to paying ZERO.
> For a detailed breakdown of the factors involved, check this out: https://whitespark.ca/local-search-ranking-factors/
> For the shortcut version, this is what we did:
> 1. Fully optimize your GBP.
> Services, products, posting frequently, replying to reviews, adding tons of pics, 24 hrs open.
> 2. GET AN ADDRESS.
> Absolute neccessity… But don’t put it ANYWHERE! Find a spot that has high income, high pop density, and lower competition (If you have 30 reviews, don’t go somewhere where 5 competitors have 150+ within 3 miles of you)
> 3. Make use of a DBA.
> Don’t keyword stuff in violation of Google’s guidelines (not that they care that much…) but get a DBA for like $25 that is something like [unique adjective] Maids | House Cleaning Service [city]. This is a HUGE factor for showing up organically.
> 4. On-site Technical SEO.
> Once you’ve optimized GBP, you need to tie that to your website and make sure your website reflects your GBP exactly and tells Google’s web crawler all about you.
> 5. Location/Service Pages
> Very underrated. Google wants to see this.
> 6. Citations / Increased Trust Indicators.
> Don’t use Yext, they’ll remove stuff if you stop paying them. Brightlocal or Whitespark. You need Google to know you exist outside of your own eco-system online and are trustworthy. Get in your local directories.
> If you took this and put it into ChatGPT, you would get 80% of the way there.
> We did these, had ChatGPT walk us through it, got expert SEO advice only 2x as a guide; and we are CRUSHING.
> We FLEW to the top of Google map pack… Because 95% of your competitors aren’t doing these things.
> Now, we aren’t just ranking organically on the map pack - we are doubling down on backlinks and are ranking organically for search results (even if we don’t show up in the map pack)
> Best decision we ever made… ABSOLUTELY CRUCIAL if you are in this for the long run.
> Every successful biz owner here doing at least $50k/mo will tell you that SEO is king. Don’t wait to do it.

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Andrea Thompson** 📈Colaborador em ascensão · 👍27: Ok got another question, how you do the physical location? Because Google doesn’t allow virtual addresses  and how much is that a month?
  - ↳ **Victor Jacon:** I love this guide, I will definitely add to our checklist. Thank you so much!!
  - _(+23 respostas no thread original)_

### 480. Here's one of my favorite "secret" ways to find great cleaners, and it has nothing to do with j…
📝 **Chris Schwab**

> Here's one of my favorite "secret" ways to find great cleaners, and it has nothing to do with job boards.
> Instead of hunting for people actively looking for work, I go to Nextdoor and look for already happy families.
> Specifically, I look for families who are already satisfied with their current cleaner and aren't in the market for a new one.
> Which sounds crazy, I know. But bear with me...
> Then I reach out with something like:
> "Hi all,
> [Your Name] here! I’m so grateful to be part of such a supportive neighborhood and would love to ask for help from fellow families today.
> I run a small local cleaning company here in [neighborhood] called [company name], and we’re starting to expand, so we are now looking for wonderful cleaners to join our team.
> If you have a maid or housekeeper you absolutely love, I’d be so grateful if you’d be open to connecting us together. I’m always looking to partner with great local people who take pride in their work and who can be vouched for by our neighbors.
> Thank you in advance, it really means a lot to small business owners like me supporting our local community here!
> "
> That's it.
> And here's why this works so well:
> You're not recruiting strangers. You're getting pre-vetted cleaners that real families in your area already love. There's no guessing and they are far less risky hires.
> You're not being salesy. You're literally helping a cleaner get more work and helping a neighbor feel like a hero for connecting people. Everyone wins.
> You're building your local reputation at the same time. Neighbors who feel good about the interaction start remembering your name and start recommending you to other families who ARE looking for cleaners.
> It's one move that solves your hiring problem AND quietly grows your word-of-mouth without spending a dime on ads.
> Next time you're struggling to find good cleaners, skip Indeed. Open Nextdoor. Find the happy families Ask them a simple favor.
> It works.
> Drop a
> below if you'd try this, or if you've done something similar! Would love to hear your version.

---

### 481. This needs to be said… When you’re running a service-based business, it’s so tempting to outsou…
📝 **Kirsten Boudreaux**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1903796743508235/)

> This needs to be said…
> When you’re running a service-based business, it’s so tempting to outsource too soon, especially when your DMs are full of people offering to “handle” your marketing, lead generation, SEO, and everything in between.
> But here’s the truth: not every task should be handed off right away. It’s just as important to be strategic about when you delegate as it is to be selective about who you bring on when you start to scale.
> Now, I’m going to tell you something you probably don’t want to hear:
> Invest in your own education first!!!
> And no I don’t mean going to business school. I mean putting in the time to really learn your business inside and out.
> Understand how lead generation, marketing, SEO, client communication, finances, and systems actually work before you pay someone else to do it.
> Run your own ads (and don’t be afraid to fail).
> Build a simple website.
> Send out a few omnichannel campaigns.
> When you do, you’ll make smarter decisions, avoid being taken advantage of, and know exactly what “good work” looks like when you’re ready to delegate.
> And here’s the bonus, when you understand the systems that make your business run, you’ll also know how to fix things when they inevitably break.
> It’s not about doing everything forever. It’s about becoming the kind of business owner who leads with clarity, confidence, and control.
> You’ve got this! I believe in you.

---

### 482. wanted to share this for anyone just starting out or stressing about ads…
📝 **Shane Healy**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1979619179259324/)

> wanted to share this for anyone just starting out or stressing about ads.
> I honestly didn’t want to waste money on Facebook or Google ads before knowing my systems worked. Instead, I focused on basic local SEO in my city (which is pretty low competition).
> I also want to give credit where it’s due i found my mentor in this group, and their guidance helped me focus on the right things instead of chasing shiny objects.
> Nothing crazy:
> • Set up my Google Business Profile
> • Filled it out properly (services, service area, hours, photos)
> • Used simple keywords like “house cleaning in [city]”
> • Asked a couple early clients for reviews
> • Made sure my phone number was everywhere and easy to click
> That’s it.
> Within a short time, I started getting calls every day from people actively looking for cleaning — not price shoppers from ads, but real leads ready to book.
> If you’re in a smaller or mid-size city, I highly recommend dialing in local SEO before spending on ads. It’s slower at first, but the leads are way warmer and basically free.
> Hope this helps someone

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Alex Swetnam** 🌟Colaborador especial · 👍12: literally the easiest thing you could do, i’ve been preaching this nonstop!! just opened another GBP and we’re killing already
  - ↳ **Tony Halfon:** Congrats!
  - _(+21 respostas no thread original)_

### 483. Don’t have a blog on website and have no backlinks or citations, haven’t listed us in business…
📝 **Alex Swetnam**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1878831769338066/)

> Don’t have a blog on website and have no backlinks or citations, haven’t listed us in business directories locally or nationally (don’t judge me, been busy lol)…
> YET we are on page 2/3 of Google with a relatively new website build.
> I would assume our highly optimized GBP (which has been killer for us, bringing in organic leads by dominating map pack) and our city-specific service pages ([city] house cleaning service) are the reason.
> Would you advise this as next steps: highlight some past cleaning projects, make an awesome blog, and double down on city/specific service pages ([city] [service type])
> Dominating our area with GBP has been KILLER, hoping for similar results by dominating in search results below map pack.
> eg. instead of just house cleaning service in Brownsville, house cleaning service in McAllen, etc… do deep cleaning service in Brownsville, apartment move out cleaning service in Brownsville, New house move-in cleaning service in Brownsville, and so forth  for each city… Just an idea

### 500. How to get FREE leads from your GBP with a verified address on Google Maps We just opened a sec…

### 535. A WARNING. A long read but an important reminder. I started out as a virtual, or, as they say "…
📝 **Jaclyn Fernandez**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2140807173140523/)

> A WARNING.  A long read but an important reminder.
> I started out as a virtual, or, as they say "remote" cleaning biz 2 years ago with 1 independent contractor.  Now, I clean about 80% of all homes with this IC and I'm not "remote" at all.  I have been working CLOSELY with her, and considered her a friend, for about 1.5 Years.  I was planning on treating her to a spa/girls day when we "catch up" on our jobs.
> I just received a text from a realtor client from a job completed last September . This Realtor hired us for a pre-listing clean of a vacant home of an elderly person that moved out of state for family to take care of him.
> Long story short, my IC that I thought I could trust, and would have NEVER imagined to do anything remotely crazy as this ~ was arrested back in March for taking 3 checks in the home , and making them out to herself.  Each check over $4,000.
> As the police just released a press release just late last week, the realtor reached out to me.
> Realtor was fired by her client.  The Police dept never made me aware of this, so the realtor assumed that I knew.  All this time, of course, this IC is still working with me.  The text message from this realtor is so upset that I never reached out to her or refunded the cleaning fee.
> Now what do I do ? How do I trust again ? I'm so shaken up as I just found this out about 1 hour ago. Clearly, I will be firing her first thing in the morning.  I don't even know HOW to present this to her  professionally, knowing that she could have destroyed my local little business.
> (Realtor chose not to publicly make a post about us / Police press release does not have our cleaning biz name on it ).
> I honestly do not know what to do next.
> She has 21 recurring clients including a full schedule this week that I desperately help on, but I cannot trust anymore.
> So as a warning, one thing I've learned today... As much as you THINK you know someone, this may not be the case. It can happen to anyone.  And now, I'm stuck with a full schedule of jobs that I KNOW I cannot do by myself.   I feel that I cannot even trust again... How am I supposed to hire someone else ?
> With that said, if anyone knows of any great, trustworthy  IC's in Northern NJ, I need help. Even just temporary help.

  - ↳ **Alina Kalinina:** I have someone who takes care of a few apartments in Jersey City for me. She lives in Newark I believe and usually available i
  - _(+10 respostas no thread original)_

### 536. Friendly reminder ab marketing The best (and most successful) biz owners in the house cleaning…
📝 **Alex Swetnam**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2157562541464986/)

> Friendly reminder ab marketing
> The best (and most successful) biz owners in the house cleaning space that I have talked to all have the same thing in common when it comes to marketing...
> They know their marketing ROI, per channel.
> If your marketing is a prayer or a hopeful wish...
> That's a MAJOR red flag.
> Everyone I talk to about $30k/mo says something along the lines of:
> SEO is killing for us. The free optimization stuff (I talk about this in my recent posts)  is amazing, backlinks/citations are worth it in the long run.
> Facebook has a lower close rate, but because the cost per lead is so low - It works.
> It's the same story - Google ads... Thumbtack... Yelp... Flyers...
> The main point: No matter what marketing they are doing, they are TRACKING spend + results so that they are 100% confident that every dollar they spend on marketing is producing profit.
> Genuinely, if you focused on this one aspect of the business - you would solve a lot of headaches...
> Yes, there are other problems you will face in other areas (labor, logistics, leadership, etc)
> but LEADS is easily solved by TRACKING!!!
> Through tracking, you can see the bottleneck.
> Is it your ads? You'll be able to see that and fix it.
> Is it your close rate? You'll be able to see that and fix it.
> Is it your sales process/follow-up? Same deal.
> Our tracking looks like a Google sheet that gets automatically updated for EVERY LEAD that comes in, takes into account all marketing spend, and what leads turned into bookings...
> Then I can see, per channel, CPL, CAC, Close Rate, etc...
> If you're struggling to be profitable on the marketing/sales side, take this post and throw it into ChatGPT or Claude and ask it to help you build a system to track all marketing and sales...
> $34k last month, numbers projected this month are $40k conservatively and $45k is our stretch goal.
> We were at $6k ish 12 months ago.
> THIS IS THE BEST TIME OF YEAR FOR CLEANING BUSINESSES!!! Grow big!! Go kill it you guys!

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Harvey Le** · 👍1: Thank you for reminding me that I need to do this.
  - _(+21 respostas no thread original)_

---

### 537. Hey everyone, I’d really appreciate your thoughts on this…
📝 **Madeeha Anwar Chaudhry**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1908706293017280/)

> Hey everyone, I’d really appreciate your thoughts on this.
> About three weeks ago, we met a local realtor at a Chamber of Commerce event. The next day, he asked us to do a move-out cleaning for one of his properties. We sent him the quote, but he didn’t enter his credit card info to confirm. Since we had just met him through the Chamber and wanted to build a good relationship, we decided to go ahead and do the job anyway.
> The property was honestly in very rough shape, and our team worked hard to make it spotless. We even left a small thank-you gift for supporting a small local business. Afterward, he mentioned he’d ask the landlord to pay the same day, but that never happened.
> I’ve since followed up several times by text, voice note, and email — all with no response. We ran into him again at a Chamber event last week, and he casually said he remembered he owed the money and was “trying to get it.” Still nothing.
> Today, he met my business partner at another Chamber event and again said, “I know I owe you,” but still hasn’t paid. He also mentioned being the Vice President of the Chamber, which makes this situation even more uncomfortable.
> My partner feels we should let it go to avoid conflict, but I personally believe accountability matters - especially within a professional network like the Chamber. We’re a small, woman-owned cleaning business trying to build honest, local relationships and this kind of experience is disheartening.
> So I’d love to hear your advice - what would you do in this situation? Should I formally report it to the Chamber, or just move on and take it as a learning experience?

### 538. After a year of running a cleaning company, I understand these things…
📝 **Tatiana Trunilina**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1717574615463783/)

> After a year of running a cleaning company, I understand these things:
> Market is everything. Turns out if it's easy to hire in your market, it's extremely hard to sell your services. Oversupply of workers brings prices down in that area
> The market is better where it's hard to hire. But you are struggling to find cleaners.
> Things can be vastly different in different cities even within the same state
> When people teach you how to open and run a cleaning business, their strategies work in their specific city and will probably not work in yours.
> We are barely hanging on, servicing a handful of regular customers which we acquired during the summer peak season. We had to turn off all of our ads because they were spending more than we were making from them. We tried a number of B2B marketing strategies even in peak months with very poor results. Most other companies in my area are dealing with the same issues, and this has been going on since September.
> Now I'm thinking if I should try to move to another market where the grass is greener. I hear lots of cleaning business owners in other parts of the US make multiple 6 figures a year, especially after a year in business, but in my specific market (Texas) cleaning companies are either closing or struggling just as we are.
> Or maybe I should just go sell cookies at a farmer's market.

---

### 540. Looking for some advice from those of you who do commercial walkthroughs…

> We had two scheduled-one at a car dealership and another at a shipping facility. In both cases, the person we originally spoke to on the phone gave us a time, but when we showed up the managers on site weren’t aware or were too busy. At the dealership, the GM never told the floor manager, so we were asked to leave. At the shipping facility, our sales rep waited almost an hour, but the manager never came out, and all that happened was exchanging business cards and being told to call back.
> For those of you with more experience:
> How do you set up these walkthroughs so the right person is actually expecting you?
> Do you confirm in a specific way to avoid this?
> Or is this just part of the numbers game with cold calling, and sometimes you have to expect wasted time until you connect with someone serious?

---

### 584. Who is using the Multistep form?…
📝 **Saleem Hourieh**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1999785427242699/)

> Who is using the Multistep form?
> Did you get a higher conversion rate?

### 588. “Does BookingKoala Plan to Integrate with Dialpad for SMS Notifications?” Hello BookingKoala Te…
📝 **Camili Pro Maids Services**

> “Does BookingKoala Plan to Integrate with Dialpad for SMS Notifications?”
> Hello BookingKoala Team,
> I’ve been a long-time user of BookingKoala for our residential and commercial cleaning business, and one of the features I value is the built-in SMS notification system (which currently uses Twilio).
> Given our operational needs (multi-location, large crews, high volume messaging, strict tracking of notifications for clients, staff and providers) we are always evaluating communication platforms for reliability, cost, compliance and workflow flexibility.
> We are curious whether you have any plans to support or fully integrate Dialpad as an alternative SMS/MMS (or unified communications) provider instead of or in addition to Twilio. A few reasons why Dialpad is on our radar:
> Dialpad offers SMS & MMS business text messaging built into its unified communications platform. Dialpad+1
> Dialpad has open APIs and supports custom integrations and workflows. Dialpad+1
> For our business model — high-volume client, staff, and provider notifications across multiple service zones (Houston, Katy, Cypress, Conroe, etc) — a platform that combines voice + messaging + integrations may offer operational efficiencies.
> So our specific questions are:
> Are there any current or upcoming BookingKoala roadmap items to natively support Dialpad (or any other SMS provider besides Twilio)?
> If not, is there a developer/API workaround you’d recommend for connecting Dialpad via Zapier/Make/Integromat to BookingKoala notifications?
> How does BookingKoala evaluate alternative SMS providers in terms of compliance (A2P messaging rules, registration requirements) which Dialpad highlights in their help docs?
> From your perspective, what are the limitations or risks of moving away from Twilio (in your built-in setup) to a custom provider?
> We value BookingKoala as a central platform for our staff scheduling, billing, client notifications, etc., and adding flexibility in our messaging stack could further help our scalability and brand reputation (especially for our premium cleaning service with strict SLA, live statuses, etc).
> Thanks for your time and looking forward to your feedback.

### 589. WE DID IT!!!…
📝 **Alex Swetnam**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2109401262947781/)

> WE DID IT!!!
> AI has been going crazy lately… but figuring out how to actually use it in a cleaning business has been lowkey frustrating lol
> We use it all the time in our real estate + SaaS businesses, so I kept feeling like I was missing something here for our house cleaning biz
> Recently started messing with Claude + this thing called MCP (still couldn’t fully explain it if I tried
> ), and it finally started to click. It basically connects AI to your actual tools. CRM, booking software, sheets, messaging… etc. so it’s not just answering questions, it’s kind of watching what’s going on.
> Our cleaning biz is run by VAs, so this has been surprisingly helpful just for staying on top of things and getting a vibe check on how things are. Stuff like:
> * catching leads that never got a reply
> * noticing which follow-ups people actually respond to
> * double checking payroll vs bookings
> * bringing old convos back up that got missed
> * even listening to call transcripts and pointing out what went well / didn’t
> It’s not perfect and I’m still figuring it out, but this is the first time AI has felt actually useful for this kind of business.
> Curious if anyone else has found simple, real ways they’re using it? In your cleaning biz (or real estate or whatever biz you own)
> Side note, I got really deep into this recently bc I realized one of our systems SMTP setting were goofed and we had 45 leads in the last two weeks that weren’t contacted (that nobody knew about) which was roughly $6-8k in first time bookings in the house cleaning biz we missed out on w our avg close rate… Don’t want to think ab the LTV lost
> but that’s what put a fire under my butt to really figure out how to get ai involved here.

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Marlon Fiel** 🌟Colaborador especial · 👍28: Alex Sweetness I posted in here if we are able to connect Claude to Booking Koala so I can learn more stuff about what Booking
  - _(+22 respostas no thread original)_
