### 592. Major updates coming to Google My Business and reviews…
📝 **Francis Clase**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2039117596642815/)

> Major updates coming to Google My Business and reviews. This month looks like it's way more AI-driven:
> Key Changes in Google Business Profile
> Updated Review Policy Enforcement
> • Stronger enforcement against review manipulation (no gated or incentive-based review requests).
> • Reviews may be removed retroactively if flagged by AI or policy checks.
> Increased Review Scrutiny
> • AI now checks patterns across reviews and can remove low-value or suspicious content (even older reviews).
> • Profiles might be restricted from receiving new reviews temporarily.
> Email Alerts for Restrictions
> • Google sends notifications when review restrictions are lifted or changed.
> Focus on Complete & Accurate Profiles
> • Having consistent Name/Address/Phone and updated hours, photos, services listed is more important than ever.
> AI-Driven Content Features (rolling forward into 2026)
> • AI-generated local answers and visual formats may start showing up in local search results (based on profile activity).
> New Transparency Attributes (where supported)
> • Profiles can add things like sustainability practices, accessibility, and service guarantees.
> WHAT THIS MEANS (SUPER BRIEF)
> Google is being more aggressive about cleaning up fake or low-quality reviews.
> Business owners must follow neutral review request practices and avoid incentives or selective asks.
> Profiles with complete, accurate info and consistent activity are rewarded, especially as AI features expand.

> Let’s talk about core values, both personally and in business.
> I’ve realized I have a tendency to “lose the plot,” especially as my businesses have grown. So I’m taking a minute to slow down and reflect, and I’d love to hear from you too.
> What are your top 3 personal core values, and your top 3 business core values?
> (They can absolutely overlap.)
> Here are mine:
> Personal Values
> 1. Integrity – Be honest with yourself. Do the right thing when no one’s watching. Help others when you can.
> 2. Discipline – Follow the plan even when you don’t feel like it. Show up. Be consistent.
> 3. Authenticity – Be real. Enough said.
> Business Values
> 1. Integrity – Lead with honesty and expect the same from the people around you.
> 2. Courage – Take calculated, meaningful risks that actually move the business forward. At the end of the day this is what being an entrepreneur is about!
> 3. Service – Lean into “losing yourself in the service of others.” Be compassionate. Go the extra mile without expecting anything back. Maybe it’s my belief in karma talking, but what goes around truly does come around, and in the cleaning industry, you see this more than you’d think.
> Tag a friend, and let’s keep the conversation going!

### 765. Happy Monday Spent the weekend at Uba (my off-grid homestead) and I'm still riding the energy f…
🖼️ **Amanda Miller**  ·  🖼️×1

> Happy Monday
> Spent the weekend at Uba (my off-grid homestead) and I'm still riding the energy from it.

> This morning I'm heading out to do my monthly clean. I make a point to get out and do at least one cleaning job a month — not because I have to, but because I never want to lead from a place that's disconnected from what my team experiences every day. It's grounding in a way I didn't expect when I started doing it. That's what
> 360 Home Services is all about
> .
> Every day is what we make it. We have the power to shape our days and ultimately our lives.
> Remember — "the most common way people give up their power is by thinking they don't have any."
> Make this week yours.

### 768. Feature request Support I just posted this feature request to BookingKoala request page and wou…
📝 **Toussaint Louverture**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1885193632035213/)

> Feature request Support
> I just posted this feature request to BookingKoala request page and would really appreciate if you could go vote it up
> I attached a poll on this facebook post for us to vote
> BUt the one I believe will matter most if the one in this link :
> https://feedback.bookingkoala.com/contribute/feature-requests/e/49215/
> Feature Request
> Title: Allow Providers to View Pay Summaries (Weekly, Monthly, Yearly) with Payment Details
> Details:
> Currently, providers can only view their pay on a per-job basis. It would be very helpful if they could also see summarized reports of their total earnings by week, month, and year.
> In addition, the summary should show:
> Which jobs have been paid vs. unpaid
> The payment method used (e.g., direct deposit, PayPal, etc.)
> The exact date when payments were made
> This would give providers full visibility into their income, payment history, and outstanding balances, making it easier for them to manage their finances.

### 769. The massive cloudflare outage has impacted thousands of companies(X, Claude, Shopify, AT&T, Pay…
📝 **Jayger McGough Tomasino**

> The massive cloudflare outage has impacted thousands of companies(X, Claude, Shopify, AT&T, Paypal, Uber etc)...
> Until service is restored, here’s how you can stay on track today:
> For Business Owners / Admin Teams: All booking details can be pulled from your email inbox, because BK sends email notifications with your booking info to the admin account and to staff accounts depending on your notification settings.
> Search your inbox using keywords like:
> “Cleaning Scheduled,” “New Booking,”
> For Cleaners:
> Tell your cleaners to check their email to get their booking details, every assigned cleaning includes:
> • Date & time
> • Client information
> • Building/parking instructions
> • Add-ons
> • Notes left by clients

> She cleaned a 4-BR house from 9am to 6pm or so and uploaded pictures of a half clean home and asked to get paid the same day, even though I pay weekly and told her this at multiple points, as well as our it in her agreement. Her contract also says she needs to provide insurance and never provided her liability insurance. She actually told me she would try and get some but didn't. ### 908. [PF Cleaning Adelaide - 5 months review] Hey everyone!…
📝 **Victor Jacon**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1726411617913416/)

> [PF Cleaning Adelaide - 5 months review]
> Hey everyone! I thought it’d be interesting to share a bit about my journey as a small business owner.
> I run PF Cleaning Adelaide, with my wife helping me manage things. For a while, it was just a glorified sole-trader business, but five months ago, I decided to go all in, hiring, training, advertising, and actually scaling it into a real business.
> *Background Context*
> I’ve always wanted to own a local business, but I wasn’t sure what to start.
> I’ve worked as a marketing coordinator for nearly 7 years, so generating leads was easy. The challenge? Finding something I could learn from scratch, train others in, and eventually build into a business.
> I’m not a plumber, electrician, carpenter, detailer, or dog groomer, so those were out. But back when I lived in Brazil, I made a decision: when I moved to Australia, I would work as a cleaner.
> And that’s exactly what I did. Once I arrived, I landed a cleaning job and… turns out, I LOVE CLEANING!
> I don’t know what’s wrong with me ahaha I genuinely enjoy it!
> Anyway, I thought hiring people would be easy. I was so wrong.
> Australia is facing a massive labor shortage, with fewer immigrants and students coming in. On top of that, most people don’t actually like cleaning, it’s just a job they accept because they need to pay the bills.
> My biggest pain point has been finding decent teams to allow growth.
> Please consider I will use Australian Dolars instead of USD.
> *A quick snapshot of my current status*
> 25 jobs per week, approx $3913 per week, 7 cleaning teams, 37 new leads per week, 13 reviews on google, 4.8 stars average
> *Investments*
> Currently spending $150 per week on ADS, $120-$200 per week on a part time assistant, $90 per month on booking koala plan, insurance, hosting etc.. Nothing fancy.
> I still can't make a living of the cleaning business, so I still work as a part-time marketing coordinator.
> *Goals*
> My current goals are to reach 40 jobs per week.
> It’s been a wild five months, I have almost quit two times, and I’m excited to see where this goes. Thanks for reading!
> if you’ve got any questions (or hiring tips
> ), drop them in the comments!

---

### 911. How do you handle customers demanding to speak to the owner when you built the business up so y…
📝 **Ami Felsino**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2165648930656347/)

> How do you handle customers demanding to speak to the owner when you built the business up so you wouldn't have to deal with customers first-hand anymore?
> Please don't say suck it up and talk to the customer. I'm not interested in doing that. We all know at a certain point it doesn't make logical sense for the owner to be customer-facing.
> For context, we messed up and caused damage to a client's hardwood floor. We explained to the customer that the VA handles all insurance claims and that talking to the owner wouldn't make sense as he's never filed an insurance claim and the VA would give better guidance for the process. The customer still demanded an "apology call" from the owner, despite the fact that we gave him an $100 refund even though insurance will fully compensate them for the damage.
> I decided to not call the client because I've had a similar instance happened and it's usually just about them wanting to get a bigger refund than we already gave them. And then even after getting yelled at, the customer still wrote a 1-star review, hence me having the opinion that this kind of thing really isn't worth my time. And even if it was, I still wouldn't want to speak to the customer to be frank, because of my vision to not be customer-facing and to allocate those tasks to VAs.
> Thanks in advance.

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Baljit Singh** 📈Colaborador em ascensão · 👍35: I’ve dealt with similar situations.
  - ↳ **Bryan Griffin:** In my experience, customers who ask to speak with the owner usually fall into two categori
  - _(+5 respostas no thread original)_

> Quick SOP Video I Thought You Guys Might Find Useful

> It's a 7-minute walkthrough of the 3-step process I use to create detailed SOPs for any task in my business. Complete video demonstration where I actually build one from scratch, autogenerate the initial doc, then do live editing to get it to a finished state.
> https://www.loom.com/.../3cc7d5022c6d490ab5aec7117b583d81...
> I use this for SOPs in all my businesses and especially when I'm delegating smaller tasks to my VAs. Instead of spending hours writing out procedures or having back-and-forth conversations trying to explain what I need, I can knock out a solid SOP in about 10 minutes and just hand it over.
> The process works for pretty much anything from customer service responses, booking procedures, team management tasks, to whatever. Once you have the template down, you can crank these out pretty fast.
> Anyway, thought some of you might get some value out of it since we all deal with the same delegation challenges. Let me know if you have questions about any part of the process or if you try it out in your own business.

### 916. STRIPE DISPUTE…
📝 **David Bui**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1900777147143528/)

> STRIPE DISPUTE: FAILS
> We don't get these often, but when we do - we lose - who has had success in the dispute process?
> Details:
> Majority of the disputes have been based on our NO-SHOW CANCELLATION FEES - customers are marking it as 'service not provided' -
> Communications:
> -Booking form has the cancellation policy written before users submit their payment details.
> - Booking form checkbox accepting terms and conditions, also evident
> -confirmation email (cancellation policy written)
> -Booking SMS text reminder (policy reiterated)
> Evidence provided to Stripe:
> -We have text messages, outbound calls (all time stamped), and photos of our team physically on-site
> Conclusion: Dispute lost.
> Keen to hear what others have done to address this - We can't imagine how much more transparent and communicative, our cancellation policy can be.

## 📈 Finanças, Crescimento & Gestão

_Faturamento, lucro, churn, impostos, seguro, escala, processos/SOPs e mindset de gestão._  ·  `#negocio`  ·  **46 publicações**

### 938. BK Fam! TL;DR: BookingKoala needs better reporting, around recurring clients, cancellations vs…
📝 **Ryan Knoll**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2038466236707951/)

> BK Fam!
> TL;DR: BookingKoala needs better reporting, around recurring clients, cancellations vs. skips, technician performance, customer scorecards, and capacity utilization, so we can make better decisions on hiring, pricing, and retention. Let's get some community love for getting these things added. Use this link to show support > https://feedback.bookingkoala.com/contribute/feature-requests/e/49793/
> Sharing a few reporting features that would make a huge difference for scaling companies and massively improve BK’s reporting.
> I would love community support in pushing for better reporting.
> The bigger a company gets, the bigger these reporting gaps feel.
> I've tried building a lot of these with external tools, but they always seem janky or lack the data that BK has.
> The biggest reporting gaps are in recurring revenue, retention, and team performance.
> 1) RECURRING CUSTOMER REPORTS
> These would be incredibly valuable for tracking business health and growth.
> Would love to see reporting for:
> Number of active recurring clients
> Example: “We have 250 active recurring clients”
> Recurring churn
> How many recurring clients canceled this month
> New recurring clients per month
> Example: “We got 16 new recurring clients this month”
> MRR from recurring clients
> One-time to recurring conversion (ascension)
> Example: “Of 40 one-time clients, 12 became recurring this month”
> For service businesses, this is the heartbeat of growth.
> 2) CANCELLATIONS REPORTING (IMPORTANT: CANCELS VS SKIPS)
> A big one for us is separating cancels vs skips.
> Right now, a skipped appointment and a true cancellation can show up similarly in BK, but they mean very different things when you’re looking at retention.
> It would be super helpful to track/report these separately:
> Skipped appointments
> Canceled service / lost customer
> That distinction matters a lot when diagnosing churn.
> 3) TECHNICIAN-LEVEL PERFORMANCE REPORTS
> It would be amazing to have technician-specific reports nested inside each technician profile (ideally near their rating/performance section).
> Suggested metrics:
> Number of recurring customers actively assigned
> Customer churn rate
> How many of their assigned customers canceled or skipped this month
> Review/feedback rate
> Not just rating score, but how many customers leave feedback
> In our experience, review frequency is a strong signal of technician performance
> Example: great cleaners may get ~50% review rate, while weaker performers may be closer to ~10%
> This would make coaching and performance management much easier.
> 4) CUSTOMER-LEVEL REPORTS / CUSTOMER SCORECARD
> A customer profile report would also be really useful for retention and account management.
> Suggested metrics:
> Completed bookings
> Total spend
> Number of cancellations
> Super helpful because a small percentage of customers may cancel frequently and create scheduling/ops issues
> This would help identify top customers and problem patterns faster.
> 5) CAPACITY REPORTING (HUGE METRIC)
> This one is a big deal for us:
> Capacity / % of available spots sold (booked)
> This has been a HUGE metric in our business.
> When we get above ~90% capacity, we know we’re generally safe to:
> raise prices, and/or
> hire more cleaners
> It’s honestly a much more useful operational metric than revenue alone, since revenue can move up/down for lots of reasons.
> WHY THIS MATTERS
> Reporting features like this would help operators:
> better track recurring revenue growth
> measure retention/churn more accurately
> coach technicians using real performance indicators
> identify high-value customers and recurring problem patterns faster
> make better hiring/pricing decisions based on capacity
> Appreciate everything BookingKoala has built. They've been a big part of our growth, and better reporting would help many of us grow faster.
> What can we do as a community to push for better reporting?

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Winta Haile** · 👍2: Agree
  - _(+16 respostas no thread original)_

---

### 939. Client Acquisition vs Client Retention I've seen that most cleaning business owners stuck under…
📝 **Alex Swetnam**

> Client Acquisition vs Client Retention
> I've seen that most cleaning business owners stuck under $10k/mo are usually blind to a crucial part of every business...
> When someone can't grow past that point - it’s usually one of these two problems:
> Client Acquisition or Client Retention
> 1) Client Acquisition (getting new customers)
> This is marketing + sales + systems.
> Marketing: Are you consistently getting inbound leads every week?
> Sales: Do you know how to convert those leads into booked jobs (fast response time, confident pricing, objection handling, solid follow-up)?
> Systems: Do you have a simple process so you’re not reinventing the wheel every time a lead comes in (scripts, CRM, automations, pipeline, reminders)?
> If any one of those is weak, you’ll feel like you’re “working so hard” but still stuck under $5k/mo, relying on referrals, or having random good weeks followed by dead weeks.
> And honestly… this is where I see most people suffering. Many people can't even get past $5k because of client acquisition problems.
> Not because they’re lazy, just nobody ever taught them a real, repeatable acquisition machine...
> Instead, biz owners that I connect with are saying they were taught:
> “Just post on Facebook and hope it works”
> “Run some ads” (with no idea what to say or how to track it)
> “Referrals are the best"
> “Just do great work and people will magically keep coming”
> “Lower your prices with discount to get the sale”
> No wonder it feels frustrating!!!
> That’s not a long-term, profitable, scalable strategy...
> The worse part is that when you've been taught this - it makes you feel like you’re doing everything “right” while still getting inconsistent results.
> What's the other part of this business??
> 2) Client Retention (keeping customers)
> Retention is service delivery + communication + consistency.
> Doing the basics extremely well, every time
> Setting expectations clearly (so you don’t create “surprise disappointment”)
> Having a simple system for issues (fix it fast, make it right, move on)
> Staying top-of-mind (easy rebooking, check-ins, little touches)
> Usually, this is where people are already doing well! They have cleaners that do great (or they ARE a great cleaner), but they can't scale.
> Basically:
> Client Acquisition = how you build momentum.
> Client Retention = how you build stability.
> If acquisition is weak, retention can’t save you.
> If retention is weak, acquisition gets expensive and exhausting.
> So if you want the simple version of this business:
> Get leads → close leads → deliver well → keep clients.
> If you’ve been feeling stuck, I’d bet money it’s on the client acquisition side.
> Don't mind my oversimplification for teaching purposes!

---

### 940. 13 months in business… this was March last year vs March this year…
🖼️ **Alex Swetnam**  ·  🖼️×2  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/2080369242517650/)

> 13 months in business… this was March last year vs March this year.
> Last year (March 2025):
> Revenue: $7,005
> Net Profit: -$1,890
> This year (March 2026):
> Revenue: $29,607
> Net Profit: $10,646
> (and yeah, some of that top line is just sales tax passing through — so the actual growth feels even more meaningful when you look at it that way)
> Same business. Same market. Same us.
> Just 13 months apart.
> When we started last February, life honestly looked like this:
> • Constant stress about money
> • Saying yes to every job (even the bad ones)
> • Doing everything ourselves — cleaning, quoting, scheduling, fixing mistakes
> • No systems, just reacting all day
> • Wondering if this would even work
> It didn’t feel like a “business.”
> It felt like survival.
> Now it looks a lot different:
> • Systems handle most of the day-to-day... We spend less than 2 hours a week on this business (we have 2 other businesses we focus on in real estate now)
> • 1x full-time VA and 1x part-time VA is fulfilling the work
> • We spend more time on leadership (directing VAs on quarterly goals) and improving things based on weekly "mistakes made" reports and KPIs
> We still work hard! Just in a very different way than before.
> A few of the biggest things we’ve learned along the way:
> 1. Systems matter more than effort
> Grinding harder didn’t fix much! Building repeatable processes did.
> 2. Speed to lead + systemic sales follow-up is huge
> A lot of growth came from just being faster, persistent, and more consistent than others.
> 3. You don’t need clarity to move forward
> We were unsure a lot of the time! We just kept going anyway.
> 4. Profit changes everything
> Going from negative to solidly positive shifts how the whole business FEELS on a day-to-day. We are often emotional before we are logical. Entrepreneurship has a sneaky way of improving you as a person so that your business also improves.
> 5. BK and other cleaning biz FB groups has helped more than I expected
> A lot of small tweaks we made came from posts and comments in here. Special shoutout to the eye-opening conversations I had this past year with Michael Zielinski, Jacob Elijah, Jacques H. Bastien, and many others.
> Just wanted to share this for anyone in the early stages right now.
> It can feel messy for a while… but it does start to click - and it IS worth it to "be your own boss". I'm enjoying the mini-vacations and freedom to step away from work and not worry about paying bills.
> If you have any questions about anything we did or what changed, I’m happy to share! At this point, it feels more fulfilling to see other people win than anything else.
> God bless!

### 941. Progress report time… this month is our best ever Every so often I like sharing the biggest les…
📝 **Alex Swetnam**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1941619299725979/)

> Progress report time… this month is our best ever
> Every so often I like sharing the biggest lessons since we started from nothing 10 months ago.
> • July: ~$10k
> • Last month: ~$19k
> • This month (projected): ~$24k
> Monthly revenue has doubled since the podcast I did with Michael Zielinski in July.
> Here are my (updated) biggest lessons so far — hope they help you grow faster than we have:
> 1. “Your net worth is your network” (cringe but true)
> You will save time and money by connecting with people who are ahead of you.
> This group is full of amazing people — use it. Don’t be scared to ask for help.
> 2. Optimize… but know what you’re optimizing for
> Most people optimize for profit.
> One of my friends does $50k/mo… but works himself to the bone every day, 7 am to 8 pm. He optimizes for PROFIT.
> I optimize for:
> • LONG-TERM GROWTH (hence our track record so far)
> • PASSIVE INCOME (I played more disc golf than I worked last week)
> If I was optimizing for PROFIT, I’d be doing things very differently.
> Whatever you optimize for should fit your lifestyle and goals.
> My big goal right now is to earn equity in an alternative investment fund I’m doing marketing and sales consulting for. So ~90% of my time goes there, and my cleaning biz gets 2–3 hours a week.
> 3. There ARE silver bullets
> I’ve had multiple changes completely transform the business in 24 hours. Objection Handling, SEO, PPC, Attribution…
> If things feel way harder than they should, you might be missing something foundational.
> 4. Business is better with friends
> I don’t think I’ll go into another venture alone again.
> I love working with people, I feed off conversation, and who better to get rich with than a good buddy?
> 5. Borrow other people’s expertise
> I ask my grandma how to bake.
> I ask my coach if my technique is right.
> I ask my cleaners how to clean.
> You don’t need to know everything about the cleaning business.
> But you should know someone who knows more than you and be willing to lean on them. This community is GOLDEN and FREE. USE IT!!!
> 6. You win by not quitting
> Most people quit.
> Even if you grow slowly, if you stay committed to this for two years, you’ll be in a great place.
> ⸻
> That’s all I’ve got for now. I wish I had understood these earlier — hope they help you grow faster than I did

### 942. Postpone Feature – Does Anyone Actually Use It?…
📝 **Mark Baker**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1917535515467691/)

> Postpone Feature – Does Anyone Actually Use It?
> We turned off the Postpone feature a while back, but I see BK has made a lot of updates to the cancellation and reschedule settings.
> I’m curious if anyone here is actively using Postpone with customers.
> Does it get used much, and how does it work out in practice?
> WHY POSTPONE SOUNDS GOOD
> Customer convenience – Customers can pause their recurring series instead of cancelling. It’s simple and feels less permanent. Perfect for vacations, extended travel, or snowbirds (we are in Canada) who plan to restart later.
> Retention – The booking relationship stays alive. Since they don’t need to rebook from scratch, they’re more likely to come back.
> Slot protection – If postpone locks their slot, their recurring time is still waiting for them. They don’t risk losing their day/time to someone else.
> Reduced cancellations – Some customers who would normally cancel entirely might instead postpone. That helps keep long-term retention numbers healthier.
> Flow – Because the series is preserved, reminders still go out before the booking resumes. Customers don’t fall through the cracks.
> WHY I’M CAUTIOUS
> Blocked recurring slots – A postponed slot is reserved and can’t be sold to another recurring customer. At best, you can fill it with one-time bookings, but that’s patchwork revenue and takes extra effort.
> Lost recurring revenue opportunities – If a slot is tied up for months, you miss the chance to put in a new recurring customer who would deliver predictable revenue week after week. When the snowbird comes back, they can always get back in line.
> Unlimited postponements – Without limits, a customer could keep pushing it forward and essentially hold a slot without paying.
> SO, I’D LOVE TO HEAR FROM OTHERS:
> Do you let your customers use Postpone?
> Has it helped you retain more customers, or do you find it hurts recurring revenue?
> Would limits (like how far ahead they can postpone, or how many times they can do it) make it more practical?

---

### 945. Hey everyone…
📝 **Steve Tam**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1903732806847962/)

> Hey everyone.  I realize a lot of companies here use contractors because the cost of W-2 is prohibitive (supplies, equipment, payroll taxes, workers comp, etc.).  But when I called insurance companies, Hiscox and Next, they both don't cover subcontractors.  Let me explain.  If you have coverage with Next, if subcontractors have an incident that requires an insurance claim, their insurance must cover first.  If the subcontractor does not have insurance, you broke their policy and Next will not cover you at all.  So they are the back-up insurance policy.  For Hiscox, their insurance policy covers your company.  It will not cover contractors work at all.  So if a contractor has an incident and the owners goes after them and they don't/can't pay, the owner goes after you, Hiscox will not pay.  The subcontractor must have insurance that covers their work.  Hiscox will only cover work done by your company and it's employees (W-2).  But a lot of subcontractors don't buy insurance because they see themselves as solo cleaners and don't think about insurance coverage.  Or do you guys have a policy that contractors MUST buy insurance or you will not give them work.

### 957. Hi - cleaning company here…
📝 **Erica Ann Rader**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1917418422146067/)

> Hi - cleaning company here.

### 984. Sometimes we look at other people’s results and think we’re behind, not good enough, or that th…
📝 **Silvia Mar**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1998273457393896/)

> Sometimes we look at other people’s results and think we’re behind, not good enough, or that this path isn’t for us. I want to share my story to remind us of something important: we don’t all start from the same place, and that doesn’t make us less.
> I started with $0.
> Literally with the vacuum from my house, cleaning by myself for $25 an hour, with no business knowledge at all.
> I come from the world of cleaners, and that felt like my destiny—clean forever, work hard, and settle.
> But I refused to believe that was all I could be. I wanted more… and I still do.
> English is my second language, and honestly, I still struggle to feel confident answering calls or doing cold calls. I make mistakes, I stumble, I doubt myself—and I keep going anyway.
> It took me a full year to understand BookingKoala,
> another year to learn Google Ads, and I’m still struggling with it.
> Building and implementing my own system has taken me 4 years of trial, error, and starting over.
> I also rebuilt my website three different times with three different developers, and I’m now on the fourth attempt, still in progress. I’ve lost time, money, and patience—but I’ve gained something incredibly valuable: clarity. I now know exactly what I want and what I won’t settle for.
> Along the way, I also hurt my back cleaning. As hard as that was, it became one of my greatest teachers. Having done the physical work myself gave me a deep understanding of what this job truly takes.
> That experience is what allows me today to understand, respect, and build the right team. I don’t lead from an office—I lead from lived experience.
> Through all of this, I’ve learned something critical: having the right people on your team is essential. Not everyone adds value, and choosing the wrong people can be expensive.
> Failure costs time and money—but it’s also part of learning. Every mistake has made me clearer, stronger, and more intentional.
> Today, my business is more than revenue—it’s my ikigai.
> I hire women, single mothers, heads of household. Women who, like me, are working to move forward and create a better life.
> I truly feel that I’m contributing something meaningful to the world by creating real opportunities from a place I deeply understand and respect.
> Yes, sometimes I compare myself.
> Sometimes I see people making double or more than I have in less time, and it can be discouraging. I’m human.
> But then I remind myself:
> my starting point was different.
> My platform was different.
> My path didn’t come with advantages.
> So I choose to celebrate myself.
> Celebrate that I’m still here.
> Celebrate that I didn’t quit.
> Celebrate that every day I feel a little more confident as a business owner and as a person.
> I truly love this group because I’ve met amazing allies here—real people who share openly and make this journey feel less lonely. Thank you from the bottom of my heart.
> If you’re starting from the bottom, feeling scared or unsure:
> your process matters.
> Your growth counts.
> And continuing forward—even with fear—is already a win

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Francis Clase** ⭐Supercolaborador · 👍3: We're entering our fourth year, so I get you 100%. Our first year, we had one of our cleaners steal all of our cleaning equipm
  - ↳ **Del Cid Verónica:** I really needed to hear this today. Thanks for your encouraging words
  - _(+19 respostas no thread original)_

### 985. Here’s the secret to not wasting money on paid ads…
📝 **Kirsten Boudreaux**

> Here’s the secret to not wasting money on paid ads: (There’s no reason to be afraid of them)
> Find out who your customer segment is in your market. Here’s a quick how to.
> If you have clients collect information on who they are and make a list. Find out their age-range, average salary for their zip code, other details such as if they are married, have kids, retired, ect…
> Bonus: Find the chillest clients you have and interview them. Ask them why they booked with you to begin with, what value they get out of your service, what they love and hate about your company, and if they have hired other services in the past. Formulate your set of questions and perform several “customer discovery” interviews. Make sure you take the time to listen more than you speak and tell them to be as honest a possible. Mentally prepare yourself to hear negative feedback but trust that this is going to help you out so much in the long run. Bonus points if you offer something in return such as a Starbucks gift card, it doesn’t have to be related to your service make it novel.
> I’ve done this before and I have several OG clients I can rely on for honest feedback and helpful information. It pays to develop these relationships trust me!
> Ok once you have data create your first at set. For demographics target behaviors that the clients you interviewed had such as income level, hobbies, interests, ect… At this stage you’re going to start to see a trend.
> Run an ad set for about a week. You may get bookings but this isn’t the goal at this stage. The goal is to gather more data so you can make better decisions when investing your advertising dollars.
> Ok so now we have arrived at the fun part. You have concrete data and hopefully some conversions. Look to see what the trends are overall. Don’t be afraid to be surprised. When I started my company I assumed that my target market was younger busy professionals and parents. I was shocked when the data showed that it was actually women 55+.
> You can stop here or, perform some additionally customer discovery interviews, which I did.
> I found every person I knew in my area who was a woman 55+ and interviewed them based on what their pain points were with cleaning.
> I was shocked to hear that they often struggled to keep a clean home due to physical limitations such as back, and knee issues and time constraints. They told me that they host at their home and often want to free up their time to spend more time with their grandkids and host events at their homes. Many of them are still in the workforce but often have a higher income at their age and can finally justify (without guilt) hiring a service.
> Now you can refine your copy and demographics to match EXACTLY who your business targets. Remember a dollar invested in customer discovery and testing is NEVER a dollar wasted.
> Good luck!

---

### 986. For those who have been successfully running cleaning businesses, how do you retain your cleane…
📝 **Adam Belko**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1945924392628803/)

> For those who have been successfully running cleaning businesses, how do you retain your cleaners?
> Here in Australia, most trade jobs I’ve done had the same issue - people who don’t care much about the work, take shortcuts, lack motivation, and aren’t interested in improving, yet complain about low pay. Now that I’m running a small cleaning business and planning to hire my first cleaner early next year, I’m wondering how do you actually keep people? And realistically, how long does a cleaner usually stay?
> I feel like a big challenge is that cleaning is relatively low-skill work, so it doesn’t always attract ambitious people or those who think independently and can do tasks without me not checking everything after them. Obviously hiring process is super important to filter out those kind of people, but again, I feel like it’s hard to attract A players when margins are not so great in cleaning business.
> Some ideas I’ve been considering for staff retention:
> • Clear financial incentives — gradually increase pay as their responsibilities grow, and provide a path for career progression
> • Team-building activities so they feel part of something more than just a shift, this would also strengthen everyone’s relationship
> • Small gestures like shouting them a coffee occasionally to show appreciation
> • Performance bonuses to recognise high-quality work and reliability
> Would love to hear what has actually worked for others. What keeps your stuff happy, motivated, and reliable?

  - ↳ **Mark Lineberry:** I'm in the US and the labor market here is completely different from region to region. I'm sure it's the same there too. I'm i
  - _(+3 respostas no thread original)_

### 988. We can all take a lesson from Joe Girard…
🖼️ **Brian Powell**  ·  🖼️×1  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1431956717358909/)

> We can all take a lesson from Joe Girard.
> Who the heck is Joe Girard?
> He’s in the Guinness Book of World Records as the greatest car salesman of all time.
> In the morning when the dealership opened, there would be a line of people waiting to talk to Joe about buying a car. He sold an average of 6 cars a day. Nowadays, nobody even comes close to that.
> His success was not due to him being an aggressive salesman, but rather one simple strategy.
> Joe sent out nearly 13,000 greeting cards to his customers every month. He made sure everyone got a card from him, and when it got to be too much work he hired two full time assistants just to send cards. He would celebrate major holidays, anniversaries, birthdays, etc. With Joe’s card coming every month, his clients considered him part of the family.
> They always got the impression that Joe cared and that made all the difference.
> This simple act inspired loyalty and motivated customers to refer their friends to him.
> This is how Joe did it. No matter what business you’re in, you can use the same simple strategy to always be top of mind with your clients.
> So why aren’t you already sending cards on a regular basis? It’s probably because of the hassle involved with sending cards.
> We now have technology that now makes this effortless. You can hop online, push a few buttons, and send a real card in the mail from 1 to thousands.
> I’d love to connect and show you how you can do this.

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**

- **Mike Ziarko** · 👍1: have you done and if so what service did you use?
  - _(+5 respostas no thread original)_

### 993. Scaling to $50K a Month I was going to drop a video this week on some more AI automations I'm w…
🎥 **Jacques H. Bastien**  ·  🖼️×1

> Scaling to $50K a Month
> I was going to drop a video this week on some more AI automations I'm working on but I'll save it for the next two weeks.
> Instead, here's a clip of my interview with BK's Michael Zielinski.
> In the full interview, I talk about:
> - Building a business empire with my wife
> - How I manage teams and build systems
> - How we find our cleaners
> - When TO scale vs when NOT to scale
> - Our pathway to $50k/month
> - How (& when) we automated our business
> And I share a few personal thoughts about parenting, kindness, work-life balance, being a 9x author, working with my spouse, teaching college, and more.
> If you didn't get a chance to watch the interview, check it on on BK's YouTube channel (link in comments)

## 💬 Discussões Gerais, Mindset & Outros

_Tópicos diversos, perguntas abertas, mindset e conversas gerais que não se encaixam acima._  ·  `#outros`  ·  **170 publicações**

### 1036. Feeling blessed We’ll start next month just shy of $10k/mo in recurring…
📝 **Alex Swetnam**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1830291414192102/)

> Feeling blessed
> We’ll start next month just shy of $10k/mo in recurring. Feel pretty awesome about getting here in 6 months (we started in Feb)!!
> Biggest lesson for me has honestly been to lock in on one thing. All of my life I’ve been a serial entrepreneur, jumping from one thing to another; trying to juggle 2-3 projects at once.
> This time, I decided to let go of two passion projects of mine; and live pretty broke in the beginning of the business so I could pick up some cleanings and learn the ins & outs of this business.
> Now we’re growing steadily every month with a team of awesome cleaners and clients!
> Time to leave the business behind, and start my coaching program for $10k…. right?!

---

### 1038. Here’s some sauce…
📝 **Alex Swetnam**  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1868102453744331/)

> Here’s some sauce:
> Sending this exact text to people we cleaned for the past 6 months. I’ve sent 30 texts and booked 3, a few more being booked as we speak.
> Here’s the text:
> Hey Nicole :)We cleaned your home a few months ago, there’s $23.17 in credit that you’ll lose if it isn’t used in 2 days. Would you like to use it before it expires? This is Alex from The Faithful Cleaners btw!
> Super
> . Some ecom guy said it was higher converting than doing a 20% off offer or similar through emails… It’s been great for us!

### 1039. Do NOT Create Systems/SOPs If This Is You…
🎥 **Jacques H. Bastien**  ·  🖼️×1  ·  [🔗 post original](https://www.facebook.com/groups/bookingkoala/posts/1991130481441527/)

> Do NOT Create Systems/SOPs If This Is You...
> Hey BK! You all know how much I live for systems and SOPs. But, I've gotten a few DMs from people who I've had to tell that their cleaning business should NOT be focusing on creating SOPs/systems.
> While it doesn't hurt to create systems, I believe those kinds of businesses should be focused their efforts on other (more urgent things).
> Let me break it down.
> As always... if you have any Qs, drop em' below.

**💬 Respostas da comunidade:**
